Life of the Author
beginner
8 min
Biography of Imam al-Shurunbulali: Author of Nur al-Idah
Biographical entry on author's life, teachers, and works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam al-Shurunbulali and explain the significance of his major works in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Imam al-Shurunbulali authored both the foundational matn Nur al-Idah and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah, making him a unique double authority.

This lesson introduces you to the life and works of Imam Hasan al-Shurunbulali, the author of the matn you are studying. Understanding his background helps you appreciate the authority and place of his writings in the Hanafi school. We will explore his lineage, education, teachers, students, and especially his major contributions: Nur al-Idah and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and nisba
Read the first paragraph to note his name (Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan ibn Ali al-Misri) and the origin of 'al-Shurunbulali' (from Shubra Bulula in Egypt). This establishes his identity and geographical background.
Geographic nisbas are common in Hanafi biographical works.
2
Trace his educational journey
Follow the timeline: born 994 AH, moved to Cairo at age 6, memorized Quran, studied under specific teachers. Note the names of his fiqh teachers (al-Nahrawi, al-Muhibbi, al-Maqdisi) as they indicate his scholarly lineage.
His teachers were prominent Hanafi scholars of the time.
3
Recognize his scholarly standing and role
The text says he became a leading jurist at al-Azhar, was relied upon for fatwa, and taught many students. List the named students (Egyptian and Syrian) to see his wide influence.
His appointment as a teacher in Cairo shows institutional recognition.
4
Catalogue his major writings
Go through the list of works: Nur al-Idah (matn), Imdad al-Fattah (sharh), Maraqi al-Falah (abridgement), commentary on Ibn Wahban, etc. Note the dates of composition to understand chronology.
Nur al-Idah was completed in 1032 AH; Imdad al-Fattah was begun in 1045 AH and finished in 1046 AH.
5
Understand the relationship between his works
Recognize that Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary on his own matn. This dual authorship gives the commentary unique authority. Also note that Maraqi al-Falah is an abridgement of Imdad al-Fattah.
Al-Shurunbulali's ability to write both the matn and its commentary is rare and valuable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الشرنبلالي
اسمه ونسبه: هو العلامة المدقق والمصنف المحرر أبو الإخلاص حسن بن علي المصري، الشرنبلالي، نسبة إلى شبرا بلولة، بلدة بالمنوفية من سواد مصر.
ولادته ونشأته: ولد رحمه الله سنة ٩٩٤هـ، وجاء به والده إلى القاهرة وسنه قريب من ست سنين فحفظ القرآن، وأخذ في الاشتغال بالعلوم، فقرأ على الشيخ محمد الحموي، والشيخ عبد الرحمن المسيري، وأخذ الفقه على الإمام عبد الله النحريري، والعلامة المحبي، وعلى الشيخ علي بن غانم المقدسي.
ثم سعى إلى الأزهر مأوى الطلاب وكعبتهم، فدرس هناك إلى أن صار من أعيان الفقهاء وفضلاء عصره، وانتشر أمره، حيث كان أحسن المتأخرين ملكة في الفقه، وأعرفهم بنصوصه وقواعده، وكان المعول عليه في الفتوى في عصره، وتعين مدرساً في القاهرة، واشتغل عليه خلق كثير، وانتفعوا بعلمه، فأخذ عنه الفقه جماعة من المصريين منهم: العلامة أحمد العجمي، والسيد أحمد الحموي، والشيخ شاهين الأرمناوي، وأخذ عنه من الشاميين العلامة إسماعيل النابلسي.
تصانيفه: له رحمه الله تصانيف كثيرة، ما بين رسائل صغيرة، وتحريرات، ومصنفات واسعة، منها: نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح الذي بدأ بتأليفه سنة (١٠٣٢هـ) وكان انتهاء تأليفه يوم الجمعة المبارك رابع عشر من جمادى الأولى بذلك العام.
إمداد الفتاح، شرح نور الإيضاح، ونجاة الأرواح الذي بدأ بجمعه في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول سنة (١٠٤٥هـ) وختم جمعه في المسودة بختام شهر رجب الحرام بذلك العام، وقد وافق الفراغ من تبيض هذا الشرح في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول وهو الثاني عشر يوم الخميس المبارك سنة (١٠٤٦هـ).
مختصر إمداد الفتاح المسمى بمراقي الفلاح الذي ابتدأ باختصاره من الإمداد في أواخر شهر جمادى الآخرة وفرغ منه في أوائل شهر رجب سنة (١٠٥٤هـ).
وشرح منظومة ابن وهبان في الفقه.
ومراقي السعادات من علمي التوحيد والعبادات.
وغنية ذوي الأحكام في بغية درر الحكام، وهو شرح درر الحكام شرح غرر الأحكام، وغيرها.
Translation of al-Shurunbulali: His name and lineage: He is the verifying scholar, author, and editor, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan ibn Ali al-Misri, al-Shurunbulali, attributed to Shubra Bulula, a town in al-Munufiyyah in the countryside of Egypt. His birth and upbringing: He was born, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 994 AH, and his father brought him to Cairo when he was about six years old. He memorized the Quran and began studying the sciences. He read under Shaykh Muhammad al-Hamawi, Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Misiri, and studied fiqh under Imam Abdullah al-Nahrawi, al-Allama al-Muhibbi, and Shaykh Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi. Then he went to al-Azhar, the shelter and gathering place of students, and studied there until he became one of the foremost jurists and distinguished scholars of his time. His reputation spread, as he had the best aptitude in fiqh among the later scholars, and the most knowledge of its texts and principles. He was relied upon for fatwa in his time, and was appointed as a teacher in Cairo. Many students studied under him and benefited from his knowledge. A group of Egyptians took fiqh from him, including al-Allama Ahmad al-Ajami, al-Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi, and Shaykh Shahin al-Armanawi. Among the Syrians, al-Allama Ismail al-Nabulsi studied under him. His works: He, may Allah have mercy on him, has many works, including small treatises, refined editions, and comprehensive compilations. Among them: Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah, which he began composing in the year 1032 AH, and its completion was on the blessed Friday, the 14th of Jumada al-Ula of that year. Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah, which he began compiling in the middle of Rabi al-Awwal 1045 AH, and finished its draft at the end of Rajab al-Haram of that year. The final copying of this commentary was completed in the middle of Rabi al-Awwal, the 12th, on blessed Thursday, 1046 AH. Mukhtasar Imdad al-Fattah, called Maraqi al-Falah, which he began abridging from Imdad at the end of Jumada al-Akhirah and finished at the beginning of Rajab 1054 AH. Also, a commentary on Ibn Wahban's poetic treatise on fiqh. Maraqi al-Sa'adat min Ilm al-Tawhid wa al-Ibadat. And Ghunyat Dhuwi al-Ahkam fi Bughyat Durar al-Hukkam, which is a commentary on Durar al-Hukkam, a commentary on Ghurar al-Ahkam, and others.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on the life of Imam Hasan al-Shurunbulali, the author of Nur al-Idah. The biography is structured in four parts: his name and lineage, his birth and education, his scholarly career and students, and his major works. The passage establishes his credentials as a leading Hanafi jurist of his time, highlighting his deep knowledge of fiqh texts and principles, his role as a mufti, and his teaching at al-Azhar. It also lists his key writings, most notably Nur al-Idah (a foundational matn in Hanafi fiqh) and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah (the very book the reader is studying). The dates given for his works help situate them historically. The biography is important for students to understand the authority of the author and the place of his works within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
الشرنبلالي (al-Shurunbulali): Nisba referring to Shubra Bulula, a town in the Menoufia region of Egypt; the author's familial/locational identifier.
نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح (Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah): A foundational matn (text) in Hanafi fiqh covering rulings on ibadat, authored by al-Shurunbulali.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): A detailed commentary (sharh) by al-Shurunbulali on his own matn Nur al-Idah, explaining the rulings with proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which year did al-Shurunbulali complete the composition of Nur al-Idah?
A) 1032 AH
B) 1045 AH
C) 1046 AH
D) 1054 AH

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Shurunbulali was a towering Hanafi scholar who authored both a foundational matn and its authoritative commentary, demonstrating the depth of his mastery.

Life of the Author
beginner
6 min
Biography of Imam al-Shurunbulali: The Author of Nur al-Idah
Introduces the author's life, education, works, and scholarly praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Shurunbulali and explain why he is a central authority in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Imam al-Shurunbulali was the preeminent Hanafi jurist of his time, author of the foundational matn Nur al-Idah.

This lesson introduces the life, education, works, and scholarly praise of Imam al-Shurunbulali, the author of the two texts we are studying: Nur al-Idah and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah. Understanding his biography establishes the authority and context of these works within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and nisba
The nisba al-Shurunbulali indicates his ancestral village, Shubra Bulula in Egypt. This geographical attribution roots him in the Egyptian Hanafi tradition.
The nisba is a marker of origin, not a tribal name.
2
Trace his early education and key teachers
He memorized Quran as a child, then studied under prominent scholars including Muhammad al-Hamawi, Abd al-Rahman al-Misiri, Abdullah al-Nahriri, and Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi. This shows his training in a variety of Islamic sciences.
His teachers were established Hanafi authorities of the time.
3
Map his academic career at al-Azhar
He studied at al-Azhar, eventually becoming one of its leading jurists and a teacher. He was appointed as a mufti and was relied upon for fatwa in Egypt.
Al-Azhar was the center of learning; his selection as mufti indicates high competence.
4
List his major works with dates
His most famous works are Nur al-Idah (1032 AH), Imdad al-Fattah (1046 AH), and Maraqi al-Falah (1054 AH). The dates show a productive scholarly career spanning decades.
Nur al-Idah is a concise matn; its commentary Imdad al-Fattah is a detailed sharh.
5
Understand the scholarly praise and legacy
Al-Muhibbi described him as 'the lamp of al-Azhar' and praised his mastery. He died in 1069 AH at about 75 years of age, leaving a lasting impact on Hanafi fiqh.
Such praise establishes his authority as a reliable source for fatwa.

Source Text

ترجمة الشرنبلالي

اسمه ونسبه: هو العلامة المدقق والمصنف المحرر أبو الإخلاص حسن بن علي المصري، الشرنبلالي، نسبة إلى شبرا بلولة، بلدة بالمنوفية من سواد مصر.

ولادته ونشأته: ولد رحمه الله سنة ٩٩٤هـ، وجاء به والده إلى القاهرة وسنه قريب من ست فحفظ القرآن، وأخذ في الاشتغال بالعلوم، فقرأ على الشيخ محمد الحموي، والشيخ عبد الرحمن المسيري، وأخذ الفقه على الإمام عبد الله النحريري، والعلامة المحبي، وعلى الشيخ علي بن غانم المقدسي. ثم سعى إلى الأزهر مأوى الطلاب وكعبتهم، فدرس هناك إلى أن صار من أعيان الفقهاء وفضلاء عصره، وانتشر أمره، حيث كان أحسن المتأخرين ملكة في الفقه، وأعرفهم بنصوصه وقواعده، وكان المعول عليه في الفتوى في عصره، وتعين مدرساً في القاهرة، واشتغل عليه خلق كثير، وانتفعوا بعلمه، فأخذ عنه الفقه جماعة من المصريين منهم: العلامة أحمد العجمي، والسيد أحمد الحموي، والشيخ شاهين الأرمناوي، وأخذ عنه من الشاميين العلامة إسماعيل النابلسي.

تصانيفه: له رحمه الله تصانيف كثيرة، ما بين رسائل صغيرة، وتحريرات، ومصنفات واسعة، منها: نور الإيضاح ونجاة الأرواح الذي بدأ بتأليفه سنة (١٠٣٢هـ) وكان انتهاء تأليفه يوم الجمعة المبارك رابع عشر من جمادى الأولى بذلك العام. إمداد الفتاح، شرح نور الإيضاح، ونجاة الأرواح الذي بدأ بجمعه في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول سنة (١٠٤٥هـ) وختم جمعه في المسودة بختام شهر رجب الحرام بذلك العام، وقد وافق الفراغ من تبيض هذا الشرح في منتصف شهر ربيع الأول وهو الثاني عشر يوم الخميس المبارك سنة (١٠٤٦هـ). مختصر إمداد الفتاح المسمى بمراقي الفلاح الذي ابتدأ باختصاره من الإمداد في أواخر شهر جمادى الآخرة وفرغ منه في أوائل شهر رجب سنة (١٠٥٤هـ). وشرح منظومة ابن وهبان في الفقه. ومراقي السعادات من علمي التوحيد والعبادات. وغنية ذوي الأحكام في بغية درر الحكام، وهو شرح درر الحكام شرح غرر الأحكام، وغيرها.

ثناء العلماء عليه: قال المحبي في رحلته إلى مصر والشيخ العمدة الحسن الشرنبلالي مصباح الأزهر، وكوكبه المنير المتلألئ، لو رآه صاحب السراج الوهاج لاقتبس من نوره، أو صاحب الظهيرة لاختفى عند ظهوره، أو ابن الحسن لأحسن الثناء عليه، أو أبو يوسف لأجله ولم يأسف على غيره ولم يلتفت إليه عمدة أرباب الخلاف وعده أصحاب الاختلاف، صاحب التحريرات والرسائل التي فاقت أنفع الوسائل، مبدي الفضائل بإيضاح تقريره، ومحيي الأفهام بدر غرر تحريره، نقال المسائل الدينية، وموضح المعضلات اليقينية، صاحب خلق حسن وفصاحة ولَسَن، وكان أحسن فقهاء زمانه.

وفاته: كانت وفاته رحمه الله يوم الجمعة بعد صلاة العصر الحادي والعشرين من شهر رمضان، سنة تسع وستين وألف عن نحو خمس وسبعين سنة.

انظر ترجمته في خلاصة الأثر للمحبي (٨٣/٢-٩٣)، وهدية العارفين (٢٩٢/١-٤٩٢)، ومعجم المؤلفين (٥٧٥/١).
Translation of al-Shurunbulali: His name and lineage: He is the scrutinizing scholar and author, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan ibn Ali al-Misri, al-Shurunbulali, attributed to Shubra Bulula, a town in al-Menoufia in rural Egypt. His birth and upbringing: He was born, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 994 AH, and his father brought him to Cairo when he was about six years old, so he memorized the Quran and began engaging in the sciences. He studied under Shaykh Muhammad al-Hamawi, Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Misiri, and took fiqh from Imam Abdullah al-Nahriri, al-Allama al-Muhibbi, and Shaykh Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi. Then he went to al-Azhar, the refuge and Kaaba of students, and studied there until he became one of the prominent jurists and distinguished scholars of his time, and his fame spread. He was the best of the later jurists in mastery of fiqh, the most knowledgeable of them in its texts and principles, and he was relied upon for fatwa in his time. He was appointed as a teacher in Cairo, and many people studied under him and benefited from his knowledge. A group of Egyptians took fiqh from him, including: al-Allama Ahmad al-Ajami, Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi, Shaykh Shahin al-Armanawi, and from the Syrians, al-Allama Ismail al-Nabulsi. His works: He, may Allah have mercy on him, has many works, between small treatises, critical editions, and extensive compositions, including: Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah, which he began writing in the year 1032 AH, and its completion was on the blessed Friday, the 14th of Jumada al-Ula of that year. Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah wa Najat al-Arwah, which he began compiling in the middle of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 1045 AH, and he finished its compilation in draft at the end of the sacred month of Rajab of that year. The completion of the fair copy of this commentary coincided with the middle of Rabi' al-Awwal, which was the 12th, on the blessed Thursday, of the year 1046 AH. The abridgment of Imdad al-Fattah called Maraqi al-Falah, which he began abridging from Imdad in late Jumada al-Akhirah and finished in early Rajab of the year 1054 AH. And a commentary on the versification of Ibn Wahban in fiqh. And Maraqi al-Sa'adat min Ilm al-Tawhid wa al-Ibadat. And Ghunyat Dhuwi al-Ahkam fi Bughyat Durar al-Hukkam, which is a commentary on Durar al-Hukkam, which is a commentary on Ghurar al-Ahkam, and others. Praise of scholars upon him: al-Muhibbi said in his journey to Egypt: 'Shaykh al-Umdah al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali is the lamp of al-Azhar and its luminous, shining star. If the owner of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj had seen him, he would have borrowed from his light; or the owner of al-Zuhaira, he would have hidden at his appearance; or Ibn al-Hasan, he would have praised him well; or Abu Yusuf, he would have exalted him and not regretted [leaving] others nor paid attention to them. He is the chief of the masters of disagreement and was counted by the partisans of difference. He is the author of critical editions and treatises that surpassed the most beneficial of means, the manifestor of virtues through the clarification of his exposition, the reviver of intellects through the pearl of his finely written lines, the transmitter of religious issues, and the clarifier of certain difficulties. He had good character, eloquence, and fluency, and he was the best of the jurists of his time.' His death: His death, may Allah have mercy on him, was on Friday after the afternoon prayer, the 21st of Ramadan, in the year 1069 AH, at about seventy-five years of age. See his biography in Khulasat al-Athar by al-Muhibbi (vol. 2 pp. 83-93), Hadiyat al-Arifin (vol. 1 pp. 292-492), and Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (vol. 1 p. 575).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author, Imam al-Shurunbulali, as found at the beginning of Imdad al-Fattah. It begins by stating his full name and lineage: Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan ibn Ali al-Misri, with the nisba al-Shurunbulali referring to his ancestral village in Egypt. The text then details his birth in 994 AH (significant because it places him in the late 10th/early 11th century AH). He came to Cairo as a child, memorized the Quran, and studied under notable scholars including Muhammad al-Hamawi and Abd al-Rahman al-Misiri. His primary fiqh teachers were Abdullah al-Nahriri and al-Muhibbi, among others. He later attended al-Azhar, where he became a leading jurist and was appointed as a teacher. The text emphasizes his mastery of Hanafi fiqh and his role as the foremost authority for fatwa in Egypt. His students included prominent Egyptians and Syrians. The passage then lists his major works, most notably Nur al-Idah (a concise fiqh manual) and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah, along with other works like Maraqi al-Falah. It includes precise dates for the composition and completion of these works, which is valuable for historical and textual study. The biography continues with a florid eulogy from al-Muhibbi, praising his scholarly stature. Finally, it records his death on 21 Ramadan 1069 AH at age 75. This biography establishes the authority of the author and the importance of his works within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الشرنبلالي (al-Shurunbulali): A nisba (attribution) indicating the author's ancestral village, Shubra Bulula in the Minufiyya province of Egypt.
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh (matn) authored by al-Shurunbulali, widely used as a foundational text.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): The commentary (sharh) written by al-Shurunbulali himself on his own matn Nur al-Idah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which year was al-Shurunbulali born?

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Shurunbulali (d. 1069 AH) was a leading Hanafi jurist, author of Nur al-Idah and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah, and his works are cornerstone texts for Hanafi fiqh study.

Life of the Author
beginner
6 min
Who is Imam al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali?
Praise of the scholar and his death date.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Imam al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali and explain his significance as the author of Nur al-Idah.

Core Idea
Al-Shurunbulali: the lamp of al-Azhar and author of the foundational matn Nur al-Idah.

Before we dive into the rulings of Nur al-Idah, it is essential to know its author. This passage from the commentary praises Imam al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali, establishing his credentials as a leading Hanafi jurist. Understanding his scholarly stature helps us appreciate the authority of his matn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the praise and note the titles: 'al-Shaykh al-‘Umdah' and 'Misbah al-Azhar'.
He is al-Hasan ibn ‘Ammar al-Shurunbulali.
2
Analyze the praise
Observe how the author compares him to earlier luminaries like the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Zahira, etc.
This suggests his high rank in fiqh.
3
Note his works
The text mentions his 'Tahrirat' and 'Rasa’il'—these include Nur al-Idah.
He is a prolific Hanafi author.
4
Confirm his death date
The passage gives the exact date: 21 Ramadan 1069 AH, at about 75 years.
That places his birth around 994 AH.

ثناء العلماء عليه: قال المحبي في رحلته إلى مصر والشيخ العمدة الحسن الشرنبلالي مصباح الأزهر، وكوكبه المنير المتلألئ، لو رآه صاحب السراج الوهاج لاقتبس من نوره، أو صاحب الظهيرة لاختفى عند ظهوره، أو ابن الحسن لأحسن الثناء عليه، أو أبو يوسف لأجله ولم يأسف على غيره ولم يلتفت إليه عمدة أرباب الخلاف وعده أصحاب الاختلاف، صاحب التحريرات والرسائل التي فاقت أنفع الوسائل، مبدي الفضائل بإيضاح تقريره، ومحيي الأفهام بدر غرر تحريره، نقال المسائل الدينية، وموضح المعضلات اليقينية، صاحب خلق حسن وفصاحة ولَسَن، وكان أحسن فقهاء زمانه. وفاته: كانت وفاته رحمه الله يوم الجمعة بعد صلاة العصر الحادي والعشرين من شهر رمضان، سنة تسع وستين وألف عن نحو خمس وسبعين سنة. انظر ترجمته في خلاصة الأثر للمحبي (83/2-93) ، وهدية العارفين (292/1-492)، ومعجم المؤلفين (575/1).
Praise of scholars upon him: Al-Muhibbi said in his journey to Egypt: 'The grand master al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali, the lamp of the Azhar, and its shining brilliant star. If the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj saw him, he would have borrowed from his light; or the author of al-Zahira, he would have disappeared at his appearance; or Ibn al-Hasan, he would have praised him; or Abu Yusuf, he would have favored him and not regretted over anyone else nor paid attention to him. The chief of the people of disagreement, counted by the people of dissent, author of the Tahrirat and treatises that surpass the most beneficial means, manifesting virtues by clarifying his exposition, reviving minds with the full moon of his splendid editing. A conveyor of religious issues, clarifier of certain difficulties, possessor of good character and eloquence and tongue. He was the best of the jurists of his time. His death: His death—may Allah have mercy on him—was on Friday after the afternoon prayer, the twenty-first of the month of Ramadan, in the year 1069 AH, at about seventy-five years. See his biography in Khulasat al-Athar by al-Muhibbi (2/83-93), Hadiyyat al-Arifin (1/292-492), and Mu'jam al-Muallifin (1/575).'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction praising the scholar al-Hasan al-Shurunbulali, a prominent Hanafi faqih and author of Nur al-Idah. It cites al-Muhibbi's praise, comparing him to earlier luminaries. The text establishes his credentials as a leading jurist of his time, emphasizing his mastery of fiqh, his scholarly works, and his virtuous character. The death notice confirms he died in 1069 AH at about 75 years, which places his birth around 994 AH. This biography serves to affirm the authority of the matn (Nur al-Idah) and the commentary that follows.

Key Terms
الشرنبلالي (al-Shurunbulali): A nisbah referring to a town in Egypt; al-Hasan ibn 'Ammar al-Shurunbulali is the author of the matn 'Nur al-Idah'.
مصباح الأزهر (Misbah al-Azhar): A metaphor: 'the lamp of al-Azhar', indicating he was a guiding light of the prestigious al-Azhar mosque/university.

The Author's Self-Introduction: Name, Lineage, and Hanifi/Hanafi Distinction
Biographical introduction of the author by himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's full name and lineage and explain the difference between 'Hanifi' and 'Hanafi' as used by the author.

Core Idea
The author distinguishes 'Hanifi' (the tolerant religion of Ibrahim) from 'Hanafi' (the school of Abu Hanifa).

Al-Shurunbulali begins his work with a formal self-introduction, identifying his name, lineage, and madhhab affiliation. He also clarifies an important terminological distinction that helps avoid confusion between the religion of Islam (Hanifiyyah) and the Hanafi school of law. This introductory passage sets the stage for the entire treatise by grounding the reader in the author's identity and the scholarly tradition he follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's name and lineage
Locate the full name: Hasan ibn Ammar ibn Ali ibn Yusuf, his teknonym Abu al-Ikhlas, his nisbah al-Wafani, al-Shurunbulali, and al-Hanafi. Note how these indicate his path, place, and school.
The author uses multiple identifiers common in Islamic biographical tradition.
2
Understand the definition of 'al-Āl'
The author specifies that 'al-Āl' (family) is restricted to nobles and important people, not commoners like cobblers. This is a linguistic clarification relevant to the context of blessing the Prophet's family.
This definition affects how we understand later supplications.
3
Recognize the rhetorical device bara'at al-istihlal
The phrase 'al-tahirin' (the pure ones) is identified as a beautiful opening that hints at the topic of purity in the text.
This shows the author's literary skill in composing the introduction.
4
Distinguish between 'Hanifi' and 'Hanafi'
The author explicitly states: 'al-din hanifi, wa al-madhhab hanafi' — the religion is Hanifi (the straight path of Ibrahim), the school is Hanafi (followers of Abu Hanifa). He cites the hadith 'I was sent with the tolerant Hanifiyyah' as evidence.
Imam Abu Hanifa himself is Hanifi (follower of the religion), not Hanafi (follower of the school). Imam al-Shafi'i is also Hanifi.
5
Note the author's self-deprecating titles
He calls himself 'al-'abd al-faqir' (the poor servant) and 'al-dhalil' (the lowly) as a sign of humility before Allah.
Such humility is a common feature of Islamic scholarly introductions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ العَبْدُ الفَقِيرُ إلَى مَوْلاهُ الغَنِي، أبو الإخلاص حَسَنُ الوَفَانِي الشرنبلالي الحنفي. وأراد بالتعميم التعميم على الآل. قاله العلامة «شهاب الدين النقشبندي». وهـو مخصوص بالأشراف وألي الخطر والشأن. فلا يقال: آل الإسكاف والحايك، فيقال: آل العباس، ولـمـا تـصـور فرعون بصورة الأشراف قيل: آل فرعون وآل النبي هم: المؤمنون؛ لأن آل الأنبياء متبعوهم، كذا في منهاج الضوء » . ( الطاهرين) عن الأدناس كلها، حسية ومعنوية، وفيـه بـراعـة الاستهلال). (وصحابته أجمعين)، تأكيد، وهو جمع أجمع، وإن كان صفة في الأصل اسم تفضيل، فإن قولنا: ا قرأت الكتاب أجمع معناه: أتم جمعاً في قراءتي من كل شيء، نقل إلى معنى الجمع. (قال الـعـبـد) الذليل، ( الفقير، إلى مولاه الغني الجليل عن كل شيء، إذ هو موجد الكائنات، وهي المفتقرة إليه بأسرها. (أبو الإخلاص كنيتـه مـن سـاداتنا بني الوفاء، أعاد الله علينـا مـن بـركـاتـهم ومددهـم، وشهرتهم وظهور كراماتهم تغني عن ذكر ألقابهم أدام الله تنزيل البركات، والفيض والنفحات بأنفاسهم، وسر أسلافهم على المسلمين، خصوصاً وفاء النيل) السعيد بمحروسة مصــر (۳)، لدفــع الضرر والإصر ) عن المخلوقات، لإيجاد الرزق بالزرع، وحصول الأقوات بدوام الأوقات (حسن) بن عمار بن علي بن يوسف ( الوفائي) () ، طريقة ( الشرنبلالي)، بلداً (الحنفي) مذهباً، النسبة إلى فَعِيْلة فَعِلي، وإلى فَعِيليَّة فعِيلي وعلى هذا قيل: الدين حنيفي والمذهب حنفــي وقــال عـلـيـه الـصـلاة والسلام: « بُعِثْتُ بالحَنِيفيَّةِ السَّمْحَةِ » ، أي: بالملة الحنيفية، والإمام الأعظم – أبو حنيفة- حنيفي غير حنفي، ومتبع أبي حنيفة حنيفي وحنفي، والإمام الشافعي له الله ) بعه حنيفي غير حنفي.
The poor servant in need of his Rich Lord, Abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Wafani al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi said. And he intended by 'include comprehensively' the inclusion of the family. This was said by the scholar Shihab al-Din al-Naqshbandi. And it is specific to nobles and those of importance and rank. So one does not say: the family of a cobbler or weaver, rather one says: the family of al-Abbas. And since Pharaoh appeared in the form of nobles, it was said: the family of Pharaoh. And the family of the Prophet are the believers; because the families of the prophets are their followers, as in Minhaj al-Daw. (The pure ones) from all impurities, sensory and spiritual, and it contains the rhetorical device of husn al-istihlal (beautiful introduction). (And all his companions), an emphasis, and it is the plural of ajma', even though it is originally an adjective, a superlative noun, for our saying: 'I read the book ajma'' means: I achieved the most complete reading of it, transferred to the meaning of totality. (The servant) the lowly, (the poor), to his Rich Lord, the Majestic from all things, for He is the existentiator of all creatures, and they are in need of Him entirely. (Abu al-Ikhlas), his teknonym, from our masters the Bani al-Wafa, may Allah return upon us from their blessings and their support, and their fame and the appearance of their miracles suffice from mentioning their titles, may Allah perpetually send down blessings, effusion, and breaths by their breaths, and the secret of their predecessors upon the Muslims, especially the wafa of the Nile, the happy in protected Egypt, to repel harm and burden from creatures, to provide sustenance through cultivation, and obtain provisions continuously. (Hasan) ibn Ammar ibn Ali ibn Yusuf (al-Wafani) by path, (al-Shurunbulali) by place, (al-Hanafi) by school. The ratio is to fa'ilah as fa'li, and to fa'iliyyah as fa'ili; and upon this it is said: the religion is Hanifi and the school is Hanafi, and he, peace be upon him, said: 'I was sent with the tolerant Hanifiyyah,' i.e., the Hanifi religion, and the great Imam – Abu Hanifa – is Hanifi not Hanafi, and the follower of Abu Hanifa is Hanifi and Hanafi, and Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, is Hanifi not Hanafi.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is the author's self-introduction. He identifies himself as 'the poor servant' abu al-Ikhlas Hasan al-Wafani al-Shurunbulali al-Hanafi. He clarifies that the command 'include comprehensively' applies specifically to noble families, not commoners. He then explains the term 'al-tahirin' (the pure ones) as a rhetorical device (husn al-istihlal) that fits the context. He emphasizes the grammatical point that 'ajma'in' is a plural emphatic. He elaborates on his own lineage, mentioning his father and grandfather, and clarifies the distinction between 'Hanifi' (pertaining to the religion of Prophet Ibrahim) and 'Hanafi' (pertaining to the school of Imam Abu Hanifa). He cites the hadith 'I was sent with the tolerant Hanifiyyah' to show that the religion is Hanifi, while the madhhab is Hanafi.

Key Terms
الحنيفية (al-hanifiyyah): The straight and tolerant religion of Ibrahim and of Islam; used here to distinguish the religion from the Hanafi madhhab.
براعة الاستهلال (bara'at al-istihlal): A rhetorical device where the author hints at the subject matter in the opening phrases.
الآل (al-al): Family, but here specifically the author defines it as limited to nobles and important people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'Hanifi' refers to the religion of Ibrahim (Islam), and 'Hanafi' refers to the school of Abu Hanifa.
C) 'Hanifi' refers to the school of Abu Hanifa, and 'Hanafi' refers to the religion.
D) 'Hanifi' is used only for the Prophet, while 'Hanafi' is for all Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shurunbulali's introduction establishes his identity and clarifies the crucial terminological distinction between the religion (Hanifi) and the school (Hanafi).

Imam Abu Hanifa’s Tawaqquf: The Principle of Withholding Judgment
List of fourteen matters where Imam Abu Hanifa withheld judgement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of tawaqquf and identify its significance in Hanafi fiqh methodology.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa's 'I do not know' is not ignorance — it is the height of scholarly caution.

In this lesson, we explore a lesser-known but deeply instructive aspect of Imam Abu Hanifa's methodology: his practice of tawaqquf — withholding a definitive ruling when evidence was inconclusive. This passage from Ibn Abidin's Hashiya lists fourteen specific issues where the Imam refrained from giving a final verdict. Understanding tawaqquf reveals the intellectual honesty and epistemic rigor that characterize the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the concept of tawaqquf
Define tawaqquf as withholding judgment due to lack of clear evidence. Contrast it with giving a fatwa or remaining silent due to ignorance.
The term comes from the Arabic root w-q-f, meaning to stop.
2
List the issues mentioned
Identify at least five of the fourteen issues: the meat of an animal fed on impurity, when a dog becomes trained, age of circumcision, hermaphrodite's urination, donkey's leftover, angels vs prophets, children of polytheists, engraving mosque walls, etc.
The passage mentions nine in the poetry plus the tenth added by Ibn Abidin about jinn.
3
Understand the reasoning behind tawaqquf
For each issue, recognize that the evidence was either conflicting, insufficient, or the ruling depended on variables (like the trainer's judgment for the dog). The Imam preferred silence over speculation.
Tawaqquf is a methodological decision, not a sign of weakness.
4
Compare tawaqquf with definitive rulings
Note that in most issues, the Hanafi school later adopted a position (either from the Sahibayn or later scholars). Tawaqquf is temporary until evidence is clear.
For example, the dog's training: the Imam left it to the afflicted person, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad specified three days without eating.
5
Appreciate the scholarly humility
Reflect on how tawaqquf exemplifies the adab of the scholar: not speaking without knowledge. This is a model for modern fatwa practice.
Imam Abu Hanifa's 'I do not know' is a powerful teaching tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله في حاشيته (۱۰۸/۳): إن الإمام توقف في أربع عشرة مسألة منها: لفظ الدهـر الدابة التي لا تأكل إلا الجلة وقيل: التي أكثر غذائها متى يطيب لحمها فروي تحبس ثلاثة أيام وقيل سبعة، ومنها الكلب متى يصير معلماً ففوضه للمبتلى، وعنه وهو قولهما بترك الأكل ثلاثاً، ومنها: وقـت الختان روي عـشــر سـنـيـن أو سـبـع، وقيل: أقصاه اثنا عشر، ومنها: الخنثى المشكل إذا بال من فرجيه وقالا : يعتبر الأكثر ، ومنها: سؤر الحمار والتوقف في طهوريته لا في طهارته، ومنها : هل الملائكة أفضل من الأنبياء ومر في الصلاة أن خواص البشر أفضل، ومنها: أطفال المشركين، وقال محمد: لا يعذب الله أحد بلا ذنب ومنها نقش جدار المسجد من ماله ومر أنه يجوز لـو خـيـف عليه من ظالم أو كان منقوشاً من الواقف أو لإصلاح الجدار. وقد نظمها شيخ الإسلام ابن أبي يوسف بقوله: حمل الإمام أبا حنيفــــة ديـنـــــه أن قال: لا أدري لتسعة أسـ أطفال أهل الشرك أين محلهم. وهل الملائكة الكرام مفضلة؟ ن جلالة أني يطيــــب الأكـــــل لـــــه؟ نبياء الله؟ ثم اللحـ والدهر، مع وقت الختان، وكلبـــهم وصف المعلم أي وقت حصله؟ والحكم في الخنثى إذا ما بال . وأجائز نقش الجدار لمـ ثم ألحق ابن عابدين بيتاً آخر فقال: ویزاد عاشرها هـل الجـني يثــــا ب بطاعة كالإنس يـــــوم المسألة
Allama Ibn Abidin mentioned in his Hashiya (3/108): The Imam withheld judgment on fourteen issues, among them: the word 'dahr', the animal that eats only al-jalla or mostly that, when its meat becomes permissible? It is narrated that it is confined for three days, and it is said seven. Among them: when does a dog become trained? He referred it to the one afflicted, and from him (and it is the opinion of the two) is leaving eating for three days. Among them: the time of circumcision, it is narrated at ten years or seven, and it is said its maximum is twelve. Among them: the ambiguous hermaphrodite when he urinates from both orifices, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: consider the majority. Among them: the leftover of the donkey, and the withholding is about its purifying property, not its purity. Among them: Are angels better than prophets? And it passed in the prayer that the elite of humans are better. Among them: the children of polytheists, and Muhammad said: Allah does not punish anyone without sin. And among them: engraving the wall of the mosque from his own wealth, and it passed that it is permissible if he fears from an oppressor or if it was engraved by the endower or for repair of the wall. And Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Abi Yusuf composed them in his saying: Imam Abu Hanifa carried his religion, saying: I do not know for nine... [poetry] ...Children of polytheists, where is their place? And are the noble angels preferred? ...or the prophets? Then the meat, the time, the dog, describing the trained one, any time it occurs? And the ruling on the hermaphrodite when he urinates. And the permissibility of engraving the wall... Then Ibn Abidin added another verse: And add a tenth: Does the jinn get reward for obedience like humans on the Day of Questioning?
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from Ibn Abidin's Hashiya listing fourteen matters on which Imam Abu Hanifa withheld a definitive ruling (tawaqquf). The lesson type is biographical, and the textual operation is critical refinement as it is from a supercommentary. The author enumerates several issues: the time when the meat of an animal fed on impurity becomes permissible, the criteria for a dog to be considered trained, the optimal age for circumcision, the ruling on a hermaphrodite, the purity of a donkey's leftover water, the comparative virtue of angels vs prophets, the fate of polytheist children, engraving on mosque walls, etc. Ibn Abidin quotes the poetic summation by Imam Muhammad's son, Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Abi Yusuf, and adds a tenth issue about jinn. The passage shows the intellectual humility of Imam Abu Hanifa and the academic rigor of the Hanafi school in admitting uncertainty.

Key Terms
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Withholding judgment or refraining from giving a definitive ruling on a matter due to lack of clear evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on how many issues did Imam Abu Hanifa withhold judgment?
A) Five
B) Ten
C) Fourteen
D) Twenty

Key Takeaway
Tawaqquf is a principled methodological stance that prioritizes epistemic caution over premature rulings, reflecting the Hanafi school's intellectual honesty.

The Colophon of Imdad al-Fattah: Date and Scribe
Colophon with completion date and scribe name

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to read and interpret a Hanafi manuscript colophon, identifying the Hijri completion date and the scribe's name.

Core Idea
A colophon reveals a book's completion date, scribe, and a prayer — a window into the scholarly tradition.

This lesson examines the colophon of Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah. Colophons are not merely historical footnotes; they ground us in the human effort behind our texts. By reading this colophon, you will learn how to identify key details that authenticate a manuscript and connect you to its transmission.

Guided Path
1
Locate the completion phrase
Find the phrase 'الفراغ من كتابة هذا الكتاب' (the completion of writing this book). This signals the end of the scribe's work.
This phrase almost always appears in colophons.
2
Extract the date and time
Identify the specific day, night, month, and year. The text says: 'ليلة الاثنين آخر ليلة من شهر رمضان سنة ١١٠٨هـ' (the night of Monday, the last night of Ramadan 1108 AH).
Dates are always Hijri in classical manuscripts.
3
Identify the scribe
Look for 'على يد' (by the hand of) followed by the name. Here it is: 'علي بن محمد الملا الحموي' (Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamwi).
The scribe may also be the author; in this case, it is the scribe copying the work.
4
Interpret the humility expressions
Note phrases like 'أضعف الورى' (the weakest of creation) and pleas for mercy. These reflect the scribe's humility and request for prayers.
Such expressions are standard in Islamic manuscripts.
5
Connect to the broader tradition
Recognize the prayer format (salawat and supplication) that opens and closes the colophon. This is typical of Hanafi manuscript culture.
Colophons are not just data; they are acts of devotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دعوة المضطرين صل على سيدنا محمد وآله واكشف كربي وحزني كما كشفت عن رسولك حزنه وكربه في هذا المقام، يا حنان يا منان يا كثير المعروف والإحسان، يا دائم النعم، يا أرحم الراحمين وصلى الله على سيدنا محمد، وعلى آله وصحبه وسلم تسليماً دائماً أبداً يا رب العالمين آمين. وكان الفراغ من كتابة هذا الكتاب ليلة الاثنين المبارك آخر ليلة من شهر رمضان المعظم قدرة من شهور سنة ١١٠٨هـ ألف ومائة وثمانية على يد أضعف الورى المحتاج إلى عفو الملك الغفار علي بن محمد الملا الحموي رحمه الله ومن دعا له بالرحمة آمين. تم بحمد الله تعالى
Prayer of the distressed: send blessings upon our master Muhammad and his family, and remove my distress and grief as You removed the grief and distress from Your Messenger in this station. O Compassionate, O Benefactor, O abundant in goodness and beneficence, O Eternal of blessings, O Most Merciful of the merciful. And may Allah send blessings upon our master Muhammad, and upon his family and companions, and grant them abundant peace forever, O Lord of the worlds, Amen. The completion of writing this book occurred on the blessed night of Monday, the last night of the great month of Ramadan, in the year 1108 AH (one thousand one hundred and eight), by the hand of the weakest of creation, the one in need of the pardon of the King, the Forgiving, Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamwi, may Allah have mercy on him, and whoever prays for mercy for him, Amen. Completed by the praise of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 709

Commentary
This passage is the author's colophon at the end of the book. It begins with a prayer for removing distress, then states the exact date and scribe. The date is the last night of Ramadan 1108 AH (corresponding to approximately April-May 1697 CE). The scribe is Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamwi, a Hanafi scholar. The colophon confirms the completion of the manuscript and includes a plea for mercy. This is typical of Islamic manuscripts.

Key Terms
الفراغ من كتابة هذا الكتاب (al-farāgh min kitābati hādhā al-kitāb): The completion of writing this book — indicates the date when the scribe finished copying or author finished composing.
أضعف الورى (ad'af al-warā): The weakest of creation — a humble self-description by the scribe/author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which month was the writing of Imdad al-Fattah completed?
A) Dhu al-Hijjah
B) Ramadan
C) Shawwal
D) Muharram

Key Takeaway
The colophon of Imdad al-Fattah was completed on the last night of Ramadan 1108 AH by Ali ibn Muhammad al-Mulla al-Hamwi.

Life of the Author
beginner
6 min
The Founders and Key Authorities of the Hanafi School
Biographical index of madhhab founders and Hanafi authorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four founders of the Sunni madhhabs and the three primary Hanafi authorities (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar ibn Hudhayl), and state their role in the Hanafi school's transmission chain.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school's authority rests on Abu Hanifa and his two chief students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

This passage is a biographical index from a Hanafi fiqh commentary. It opens with the founders of the four Sunni legal schools and then lists key Hanafi scholars. For a student of fiqh, knowing who these figures are and how they relate to each other is essential for understanding the authority behind legal rulings. The index serves as a reference for the chain of transmission (sanad) that underlies Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four imams
Read the first section: Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Note their birth/death years and key works. Each is the 'sahib al-madhhab' of their respective school.
Abu Hanifa died 150 AH; Malik died 179 AH; al-Shafi'i died 204 AH; Ahmad died 241 AH.
2
Locate the Hanafi founding figures
After the four imams, the index lists Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar ibn Hudhayl. These are the direct students of Abu Hanifa who transmitted his teachings. Note their dates and teachers.
Abu Yusuf died 182 AH; Muhammad died 189 AH; Zufar died 158 AH.
3
Note the chain of transmission
Trace who studied under whom: Abu Hanifa taught Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad then taught later scholars like Ahmad ibn Hanbal (who also studied under Muhammad). This chain establishes the reliability of the transmitted rulings.
Zufar was the oldest student, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are the main transmitters of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Understand the authority ranking
Within the Hanafi school, the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani carry more weight than Zufar's when they differ. This is because their works form the core of the school's relied-upon texts.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah typically follows Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, over Zufar.
5
Recognize the purpose of the index
This index is not just a list; it serves as a memorization anchor for the school's authorities. Knowing these names helps students locate sources and understand citations in fiqh works.
Later Hanafi commentaries often reference these scholars by name.

فهرس تراجم الرجال

تراجم الأئمة أصحاب المذاهب الأربعة

أبو حنيفة: صاحب المذهب الحنفي، فقيه الملة، عالم العراق، أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت بن زوطا التيمي الكوفي مولى بني تيم الله بن ثعلبة ولد سنة (٨٠هـ) في حياة صغار الصحابة، ورأى أنس بن مالك لما قدم عليهم الكوفة، وتفقه على حماد ابن أبي سليمان، وكان لا يقبل جوائز الدولة بل ينفق من دارٍ كبيرة له لعمل الخز وعنده صنّاع وأجراء، توفي في بغداد سنة ( ١٥٠هـ ) ودفن بمقابر الخيزران من تلامذته زفر ابن هذيل، وداود الطائي، وأبو يوسف، ومحمـد بـن الحسن، وأسد بن عمرو، والحسن اللؤلؤي، ونوح الجامع وغيرهم من آثاره الفقه الأكبر في الكلام، الرد على القدرية، المسند في الحديث اهـ . أعلام النبلاء (٣٩٠/٦). سير

مالك: صاحب المذهب المالكي، إمام دار الهجرة، أبو عبد الله مالك بن أنس الأصبحي ولد في المدينة المنورة سنة (۹۳هـ)، وتوفي سنة (١٧٩هـ)، وجّه إليه الخليفة هارون الرشيد ليأتيه فيحدثه فقال: الـعـلـم يـؤتـي فقصد الرشيد منزله، واستند إلى الجدار فقال مالك يا أمير المؤمنين من إجلال رسول الله إجلال العلم فجلس بين يديه فحدثه، مـن تصانيفه الموطأ، رسالته إلى الرشيد، وكتاب في المسائل، وتفسير غريب القرآن وغيرها .اهـ. معجم المؤلفين (١٦٨/٨).

الشافعي: صاحب المذهب الشافعي، الإمام الفقيه محمد بن إدريس بن العباس بن عثمان بن شافع أبو عبد الله القرشي، ولد بغزة بفلسطين سنة (١٥٠هـ) وحمل إلى مكة وهو ابن سنتين وتوفي في مصر سنة (٢٠٤ هـ) ودفن فيها. مــن تصانيفه المسند في الحديث أحكام القرآن اختلاف الحديث، إثبات النبوة، والرد على البراهمة، والمبسوط في الفقه رواه عنه الربيع بن سليمان والزعفراني وغيرها كثير اهـ معجم المؤلفين (۳۲/۹).

أحمد بن حنبل: صاحب المذهب الحنبلي، أبو عبد الله أحمد بن محمد بن حنبل بن هلال المروزي البغدادي، إمام في الحديث والفقه ولد سنة (١٦٤هـ) في بغداد ونشأ بها، وطلب العلم وسمع الحديث من شيوخها وتوفي سنة (٢٤١هـ)، وقد امتحن بمسألة خلق القرآن من تصانيفه: المسند يحتوي على نيف وأربعين ألف حديث، الناسخ والمنسوخ، كتاب الزهد وغيرها .اهـ. معجم المؤلفين (٩٦/٢).

تراجم الأئمة المشاهير أصل المذهب الحنفي

أبو يوسف: قاضي القضاة أبو يوسف يعقوب بن إبراهيم بن حبيب الأنصاري الكوفي الإمام المجتهد العلامة المحدث، ولد سنة (۱۱۳هـ) صاحب أبي حنيفة سمع من هشام بن عروة، وعداء بن السائب وعنه محمد بن ا وأحمد ابن حنبل، ويحيى بن معين وغيرهم، توفي سنة (۱۸۲هـ ) من تصانيفه: كتاب الخراج، أدب القاضي، الأمالي في الفقه اهـ السير (٥٢٥/٨).

محمد بن الحسن الشيباني: أبو عبد الله أصله من الشام من حرستا بغوطة دمشق ولد بواسط سنة (١٣٥هـ) ونشأ بالكوفة وطلب الحديث فسمع من معمر بن كدام ومالك والأوزاعي، وأخذ الفقه عن أبي حنيفة ثم تفقه على أبي يوسف وتوفي بالري سنة (١٨٩هـ). السير (١٣٤/٩). وفي الجواهر المضية توفي سنة (١٨٧هـ).

زفر بن هذيل البصري العنبري الفقيه المجتهد العلامة أبو الهذيل ولد سنة (١١٠هـ) وهو من بحور ا الفقه وأذكياء الوقت، تفقه بأبي حنيفة وهو أكبر تلامذته، وكان ممن جمع بين العلم والعمل وكان يدري الحديث ويتقنه، مات زفر سنة (١٥٨هـ) اهـ. السير (٣٩/٨).

أسماء الأعلام مرتبة أسماؤهم أبجدياً :
1- إبراهيم بن محمد بن المنتشر بن الأجدع الهمداني الكوفي، أحد أئمة الدين، ومن ثبت العلم، وهو قديم الوفاة ا.هـ السير (٥٥/٧).
- إبراهيم: هو الإمام التابعي إبراهيم بن يزيد النخعي أبو عمران اليماني الكوفي توفي مختفياً من الحجاج سنة (٩٦هـ) اهـ. التاريخ الكبير (٣٣٣/١).
ابن أبي شيبة - عبد الله بن محمد بن إبراهيم بن عثمان الكوفي، المعروف بابن أبي شيبة، أبو بكر، محدث، فقيه. من تصانيفه: المصنف في الحديث، السنن في الفقه، ولد سنة (١٥٩هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٣٥هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٠٧/٦).
ابن أبي :، عمران = أحمد بن أبي عمران قاضي الديار المصرية أحمد بن أبي عمران بن عيسى أبو جعفر البغدادي تفقه على محمد بن سماعة عن أبي يوسف ومحمد وهو أستاذ الطحاوي مات سنة (٢٨٠هـ)، من تصانيفه: الحجج اهـ. الفوائد البهية (ص۳۳).
ابن أبي ليلى = محمد بن عبد الرحمن: هو الإمام محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى العلامة، مفتي الكوفة وقاضيها، أبو عبد الرحمن الأنصاري، ولد سنة نيف وسبعين وتوفي سنة (١٤٨هـ) اهـ. السير (٣١٠/٦).
ابن أبي مليكة = عبد الله بن عبيد الله: هو الإمام عبد الله بن عبيد الله بن أبي مليكة ولد في خلافة علي – كرم الله وجهه - كان عالماً فقيهاً صاحب حديث وإتقان، مات سنة (١١٧هـ) اهـ السير (٨٨/٥).
ابن أمير حاج - = محمد بن محمد هو الإمام محمد بن محمد بن محمد المعروف بابن أمير حاج ويقال لـه ابـن الموقت أبو عبد الله شمس الدين من علماء حلب، ولد سنة (٨٢٥هـ) وتوفي سنة (٨٧٩هـ ) من تصانيفه: حلبة المجلـي وبغية المهتدي في شرح منية المصلي، التقرير والتحبير في شرح التحرير لابن الهمام وذخيرة القصر في تفسير سورة العصر اهـ. الأعلام (٤٩/٧).
ابن الأثير - علي بن محمد بن محمد بن عبد الكريم بن عبد الواحد الشيباني الموصلي، المعروف بابن الأثير الجزري أبو الحسن، مؤرخ ،محدث لغوي من تصانيفه الكامل في التاريخ أسد الغابة في معرفة الصحابة، ولد سنة (٥٥٥هـ) توفي سنة (٦٣٠هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۲۲۸/۷).
ابن الأعرابي - محمد بن زياد بن الأعرابي أبو عبد الله لغوي، نحوي، من تصانيفه النوادر، تاريخ القبائل، ولد سنة (١٥٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٣١هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۱۱/۱۰).
ابن الأنباري - محمد بن عبد الكريم بن إبراهيم بن عبد الكريم بن رفاعة الشيباني، المعروف بابن الأنباري (سديد الدولة) من الكتاب والوزراء، توفي سنة (٥٥٨هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٨٦/١٠).
ابن السني - أحمد بن محمد بن إسحاق الدينوري أبو بكر المعروف بابن السني، محدث، من تصانيفه: عمـل الـيـوم والليلة، مختصر سنن النسائي، توفي سنة (٣٦٤ هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۸۰/۲).
ابن الشحنة = عبد البر بن محمد هو عبد البر بن محمد بن محمد بن محمود بن الشحنة الحلبي، ثم القاهري الحنفي (سري الدين أبو البركات فقيه، أصولي، ولد سنة (٨٥١هـ) وتوفي سنة (٩٢١هـ) من تصانيفه: الإشارة والرمز إلى تحقيق الوقاية شرح الكنز في فروع الفقه الحنفي .اهـ. معجم المؤلفين (٧٧/٥).
ابن الضياء - محمد بن أحمد بن الضياء المكي، أبو البقاء، من تصانيفه المشرع في شرح مجمع وهو شرح البحرين وملتقى النهرين، توفي سنة (٨٥٤هـ ) ا.هـ كشف الظنون (١٦٠١/٢).
ابن الضياء - محمد بن ا أحمد بن محمد بن محمد بن محمد العمري ويعرف بابن الضياء، فقيه، أصولي، مفسر، من مجمع البحرين في فروع الحنفية البحر العميق في مناسك المعتمر ، ولد سنة (۷۸۹هـ) وتوفي سنة (٨٥٤هـ) تصانيفه: ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٥/٩).
ابن العربي - محمد بن عبد الله بن محمد بن عبد الله ابن العربي أبو بكر القاضي الفقيه، المحدث، من تصانيفه: شرح الجامع الصحيح للترمذي، غوامض النحويين، ولد سنة (٤٦٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (٥٤٣هـ) ا.هـ السير (١٩٧/٢٠).
ابن العماد - عبد الرحمن بن محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن عماد الدين العمادي، الدمشقي، الحنفي، فقيه، مفسر، أديب، ولي الإفتاء بدمشق من تصانيفه: هدية بن العماد، تحرير التأويل على ما في معاني أي التنزيل، ولد سنة (١٠٧٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (١١٧١هـ) [؟] - Vro -
Index of biographies of men. Biographies of the Imams, the four schools' founders: Abu Hanifa: founder of the Hanafi school, jurist of the community, scholar of Iraq, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit ibn Zuta al-Taymi al-Kufi, client of Banu Taym Allah ibn Tha'laba. Born 80 AH during the lifetime of the younger Companions, saw Anas ibn Malik when he came to Kufa, studied fiqh under Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman. He did not accept state gifts but spent from a large house he owned for silk trade, having workers and employees. Died in Baghdad 150 AH, buried in Khayzuran cemetery. Among his students: Zufar ibn Hudhayl, Dawud al-Ta'i, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, Asad ibn Amr, al-Hasan al-Lu'lu'i, Nuh al-Jami', others. His works: al-Fiqh al-Akbar on theology, al-Radd ala al-Qadariyya, al-Musnad in hadith. End. From Siyar A'lam al-Nubala (6/390). Malik: Founder of Maliki school, Imam of Dar al-Hijra, Abu Abdullah Malik ibn Anas al-Asbahi. Born in Medina 93 AH, died 179 AH. Caliph Harun al-Rashid sent for him to come and narrate hadith; Malik said 'Knowledge is sought', so al-Rashid went to his home, leaned against the wall; Malik said 'O Commander of the Faithful, from honoring Allah's Messenger is honoring knowledge', so he sat before him and narrated. His works: al-Muwatta, his epistle to al-Rashid, a book on legal questions, Tafsir Gharib al-Qur'an, others. End. From Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (8/168). Al-Shafi'i: Founder of Shafi'i school, Imam jurist Muhammad ibn Idris ibn al-Abbas ibn Uthman ibn Shafi', Abu Abdullah al-Qurashi. Born in Gaza, Palestine 150 AH, taken to Mecca at age two, died in Egypt 204 AH and buried there. His works: al-Musnad in hadith, Ahkam al-Qur'an, Ikhtilaf al-Hadith, Ithbat al-Nubuwwa, al-Radd ala al-Barahima, al-Mabsut in fiqh narrated from him by al-Rabi' ibn Sulayman and al-Za'farani and many others. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (9/32). Ahmad ibn Hanbal: Founder of Hanbali school, Abu Abdullah Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Hanbal ibn Hilal al-Marwazi al-Baghdadi, Imam in hadith and fiqh. Born 164 AH in Baghdad and grew up there, sought knowledge and heard hadith from its shaykhs, died 241 AH. He was tested over the issue of the creation of the Qur'an. His works: al-Musnad containing over forty thousand hadiths, al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh, Kitab al-Zuhd, others. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/96). Biographies of famous Imams, the source of the Hanafi school. Abu Yusuf: Chief judge Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim ibn Habib al-Ansari al-Kufi, the mujtahid Imam, scholar, muhaddith. Born 113 AH, companion of Abu Hanifa. Heard from Hisham ibn Urwa and others. From him narrated Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Yahya ibn Ma'in, others. Died 182 AH. His works: Kitab al-Kharaj, Adab al-Qadi, al-Amali in fiqh. End. From Siyar (8/525). Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani: Abu Abdullah, originally from Syria, from Harasta in Ghouta of Damascus. Born in Wasit 135 AH, grew up in Kufa, sought hadith hearing from Mu'ammar ibn Kadham, Malik, al-Awza'i; took fiqh from Abu Hanifa then studied under Abu Yusuf. Died in Rayy 189 AH. Siyar (9/134). In al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya: died 187 AH. Zufar ibn Hudhayl al-Basri al-Anbari, the mujtahid jurist, scholar Abu al-Hudhayl. Born 110 AH, one of the oceans of fiqh and the most intelligent of his time. Studied under Abu Hanifa and was his oldest student. Combined knowledge and action, knew and mastered hadith. Died 158 AH. End. Siyar (8/39). Names of notable figures arranged alphabetically: 1- Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muntashir ibn al-Ajda' al-Hamdani al-Kufi, one of the leaders of the religion, firm in knowledge, early death. End. Siyar (7/55). - Ibrahim: the Tabi'i Imam Ibrahim ibn Yazid al-Nakha'i Abu Imran al-Yamani al-Kufi died in hiding from al-Hajjaj 96 AH. End. al-Tarikh al-Kabir (1/333). Ibn Abi Shayba - Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Uthman al-Kufi, known as Ibn Abi Shayba, Abu Bakr, muhaddith, faqih. His works: al-Musannaf in hadith, al-Sunan in fiqh. Born 159 AH, died 235 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (6/107). Ibn Abi [Umaran?] = Ahmad ibn Abi Umaran, judge of Egypt Ahmad ibn Abi Umaran ibn Isa Abu Ja'far al-Baghdadi, studied fiqh under Muhammad ibn Sama'a from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), was teacher of al-Tahawi. Died 280 AH. His works: al-Hujaj. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (p.33). Ibn Abi Layla = Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman: Imam Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, scholar, mufti and judge of Kufa, Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Ansari. Born around seventy? Died 148 AH. End. Siyar (6/310). Ibn Abi Mulayka = Abdullah ibn Ubayd Allah: Imam Abdullah ibn Ubayd Allah ibn Abi Mulayka, born during the caliphate of Ali (may Allah honor his face), was a scholar, faqih, possessor of hadith and precision. Died 117 AH. End. Siyar (5/88). Ibn Amir Haj = Muhammad ibn Muhammad: Imam Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad known as Ibn Amir Haj, also called Ibn al-Muwaqqit, Abu Abdullah Shams al-Din, from scholars of Aleppo. Born 825 AH, died 879 AH. His works: Halbat al-Mujalli wa Bughyat al-Muhtadi fi Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir fi Sharh al-Tahrir li Ibn al-Humam, and Dhakhirat al-Qasr fi Tafsir Surat al-Asr. End. al-A'lam (7/49). Ibn al-Athir - Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Abd al-Wahid al-Shaybani al-Mawsili, known as Ibn al-Athir al-Jazari, Abu al-Hasan, historian, muhaddith, linguist. His works: al-Kamil fi al-Tarikh, Usd al-Ghaba fi Ma'rifat al-Sahaba. Born 555 AH, died 630 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (7/228). Ibn al-A'rabi - Muhammad ibn Ziyad ibn al-A'rabi, Abu Abdullah, linguist, grammarian. His works: al-Nawadir, Tarikh al-Qaba'il. Born 150 AH, died 231 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (10/11). Ibn al-Anbari - Muhammad ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Ibrahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Rifa'a al-Shaybani, known as Ibn al-Anbari (Sadid al-Dawla), among secretaries and ministers. Died 558 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (10/186). Ibn al-Sunni - Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Dinawari Abu Bakr, known as Ibn al-Sunni, muhaddith. His works: 'Amal al-Yawm wa al-Layla, Mukhtasar Sunan al-Nasa'i. Died 364 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/80). Ibn al-Shihna = Abd al-Barr ibn Muhammad: Abd al-Barr ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn al-Shihna al-Halabi, then al-Qahiri al-Hanafi (Sari al-Din Abu al-Barakat, faqih, usuli. Born 851 AH, died 921 AH. His works: al-Ishara wa al-Ramz ila Tahqiq al-Wiqaya Sharh al-Kanz fi Furu' al-Fiqh al-Hanafi. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (5/77). Ibn al-Diya' - Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Diya' al-Makki, Abu al-Baqa'. His works: al-Mashra' fi Sharh al-Majma' which is a commentary on al-Bahrayn and Multaqa al-Nahrayn. Died 854 AH. End. Kashf al-Zunun (2/1601). Ibn al-Diya' - Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Amari, known as Ibn al-Diya', faqih, usuli, mufassir. Works: Majma' al-Bahrayn fi Furu' al-Hanafiyya, al-Bahr al-Amiq fi Manasik al-Mu'tamir. Born 789 AH, died 854 AH. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (9/15). Ibn al-Arabi - Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn al-Arabi, Abu Bakr, judge, faqih, muhaddith. His works: Sharh al-Jami' al-Sahih li al-Tirmidhi, Ghawamid al-Nahawiyin. Born 468 AH, died 543 AH. End. Siyar (20/197). Ibn al-Imad - Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Imad al-Din al-Imadi, al-Dimashqi, al-Hanafi, faqih, mufassir, adib. Held the office of ifta' in Damascus. His works: Hadiyyat Ibn al-Imad, Tahrir al-Ta'wil 'ala ma fi Ma'ani Ay al-Tanzil. Born [1078?] AH, died 1171 AH [?] - End.
Source pages p. 735

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index (fihris tarajim al-rijal) taken from a Hanafi fiqh commentary. It opens with biographies of the four great imams: Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal—founders of the Sunni legal schools. These are standard reference biographies, providing birth and death dates, major teachers and students, and key works. For Hanafi students, the biography of Abu Hanifa is especially important: he was born in 80 AH, saw the Companion Anas ibn Malik, studied under Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, and refused state patronage, financing his scholarship through his own silk trade. His students include Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose works form the Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage then lists biographies of prominent Hanafi authorities: Abu Yusuf (the chief judge), Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar ibn Hudhayl, noting their scholarly contributions and death dates. The remainder of the index alphabetically lists other scholars relevant to Hanafi fiqh, including early authorities like Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and later commentators like Ibn Amir Haj and Ibn al-Diya'. This type of biographical index serves to establish the chain of transmission and authority of the legal rulings cited in the main text. Students of the Hanafi school should recognize these names as the foundational figures whose works are relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms
تراجم الرجال (tarājim al-rijāl): Biographical entries of notable men, typically scholars and transmitters of hadith and fiqh.
صاحب المذهب (ṣāḥib al-madhhab): The founder of a legal school (madhhab). Used for the four imams.
زفر بن هذيل (Zufar ibn Hudhayl): A prominent student of Abu Hanifa, known for his ijtihad and intelligence. He is one of the early transmitters of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Zufar ibn Hudhayl

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authority flows from Abu Hanifa through his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose works form the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Using the Biographical Index: Identifying Key Hanafi Authorities
Biographical index of scholars cited in the commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi scholars listed in the biographical index, state their contributions, and use the index to trace the chain of knowledge in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Biographical indices link fiqh rulings to their authoritative sources—knowing the scholars builds your understanding of the madhhab's foundation.

This passage is a biographical index (tarajim) from Imdad al-Fattah, listing over thirty scholars cited in the commentary. Such indices are not mere lists; they are the backbone of scholarly credibility. By learning who these scholars are, their eras, and their works, you gain the ability to assess the strength of a ruling, understand the development of the Hanafi school, and appreciate the chain of transmission that validates our fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Name and Era
Scan the entry for the scholar's full name, title, and death year. This places him historically.
Death years help determine who influenced whom.
2
Note His Specialization
Look for labels like 'muhaddith', 'faqih', 'faqih usuli'. This tells you his primary field.
A faqih jurist vs a muhaddith hadith specialist.
3
List His Major Works
Entries often mention key books he authored. These works are sources for Hanafi rulings.
For example, Ibn al-Humam wrote Fath al-Qadir.
4
Recognize His Madhhab Connection
Determine if he is a Hanafi, or a source for Hanafi fiqh (e.g., Ibrahim al-Nakhai was a Kufan Tabi'i that influenced Abu Hanifa).
Not all listed are Hanafis, but all are relevant.
5
Build a Mental Network
Connect scholars through teacher-student relationships. This shows the chain of knowledge.
For instance, Ibn Sam'ah studied under Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index (tarajim) listing the names, lineages, professions, works, and death dates of scholars cited in the commentary. Such indices are common in Islamic scholarly works to establish the credibility and chain of transmission of the author's sources. The entries span from early Tabi'un like Ibrahim al-Nakhai (d. 96 AH) to later Hanafi jurists like Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 AH). Many are key figures in the Hanafi school, such as Ibn Abi Shayba, Ibn al-Humam, and Ibn al-Shihna. The list serves as a quick reference for the reader to identify the authorities behind the fiqh rulings discussed in the text.

Key Terms
إبراهيم النخعي (Ibrahim al-Nakha'i): A prominent Tabi'i jurist and traditionist from Kufa, a key source for early Hanafi fiqh.
ابن الهمام (Ibn al-Humam): Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi, a leading Hanafi jurist and author of Fath al-Qadir, a commentary on al-Hidayah.
محدث (muhaddith): A scholar specializing in Hadith studies, including transmission and criticism.

Navigating Biographical Lists in Hanafi Texts
Biographical entries of scholars cited in Imdad al-Fattah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Hanafi scholars listed in Imdad al-Fattah and explain the purpose of such biographical lists in fatwa literature.

Core Idea
Biographical lists establish scholarly chains and authority – knowing who the author cites reveals the transmission strength.

Biographical lists like the one in Imdad al-Fattah are not mere decoration. They serve as a chain of transmission (sanad) for the rulings cited in the commentary. Each entry provides the scholar's full name, lifespan, notable works, and often a reference source. Understanding these entries helps you gauge the authority of the opinions and identify the madhhab of each figure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry structure
Each entry typically includes: numbering, name (with kunya and nisba), death date (hijri), notable works, and a source reference (e.g. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya). Sometimes a brief description like 'muhaddith' or 'faqih' is given.
Death dates are crucial for establishing contemporaneity with other scholars.
2
Recognize the sources used
The author relies on biographical works like al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (Hanafi-specific) and Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (general). Knowing these sources tells you the reliability and focus of the entry.
Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya is a Hanafi biographical dictionary; Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin covers all disciplines.
3
Distinguish Hanafi from non-Hanafi scholars
Not all scholars listed are Hanafi. Some, like Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (Shafi'i) or Ibn Qudama (Hanbali), are included because their works are referenced in the commentary.
Check the madhhab label (e.g., 'al-Hanbali') or the scholar's reputation to identify affiliation.
4
Understand the purpose in fatwa literature
These lists provide credentials for the scholars whose opinions or works are cited. They help the reader assess the authority of a transmitted ruling.
A fatwa citing a respected Hanafi authority like Ibn al-Humam carries more weight than a lesser-known figure.
5
Apply by locating a specific scholar
Given a name like 'Ibn al-Humam', scan the list for his entry, note his full name (Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi), his work Fath al-Qadir, and his death date (861 AH).
Practice with several entries to become fluent.

أخذ الفقه عن
۱۷- ابن الفضل = محمد بن الفضل الكماري: كان إماماً كبيراً وشيخاً جليلاً وكتب الفتاوى مشحونة بفتاواه ورواياتـه الله السيذموني، ولد سنة (٤٢٦هـ) وتوفي سنة (٥٠٨هـ) اهـ. الفوائد البهية (٣٠٣). الأستاذ . عبد ۱۸- ابن القطان - يحيى بن سعيد بن فروخ القطان أبو سعيد، أمير المؤمنين في الحديث، ولد سنة (١٢٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (۱۹۸هـ ) ا.هـ السير (١٧٥/٩).
١٩- ابن النجار = محمد بن جعفر بن محمد بن هارون التميمي المعروف بابن النجار أبو الحسين، أديب، نحوي، مؤرخ، من تصانيفه: تاريخ الكوفة، مختصر في النحو، ولد سنة (۳۰۳هـ) وتوفي سنة (٤٦٠هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٥٧/٩). ٢٠ ابن الهمام = محمد بن عبد الواحد هو الإمام كمال الدين محمد بن عبد الواحد السيواسي المعروف بابن الهمام شرح الهداية وسماه فتح القدير للعاجز ،الفقير، توفي سنة (٨٦١هـ ) اهـ كشف الظنون (٢٠٣٤/٢). ۲۱- ابن حجر = أحمد بن علي هو الإمام شهاب الدين أحمد بن علي بن حجر العسقلاني الحافظ المؤرخ ولد سنة (۷۷۳هـ) وتوفي سنة (٨٥٢هـ) من تصانيفه: فتح الباري بشرح صحيح البخاري، الإصابة في تمييز الصحابة وغيرها اهـ. معجم المؤلفين (۲۰/۲).
۲۲- ابن خزيمة - محمد بن إسحاق بن خزيمة أبو بكر ، المحدث، من تصانيفه: صحيح ابن خزيمة، التوحيد وإثبات صفات الرب، ولد سنة (٢٢٣هـ) وتوفي سنة (۳۱۱هـ) اهـ معجم المؤلفين (۳۹/۹). ۲۳- ابن درستویه - عبد الله بن جعفر بن درستويه بن المرزبان أبو محمد النحوي اللغوي أخذ الأدب عن ابن قتيبة والمبرد. من تصانيفه: الأرشاد في النحو، المقصور والممدود أخبار النحويين ولد سنة (٢٥٨هـ) وتوفي سـ سنة (٣٤٧هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٤٠/٦).
٢٤- ابن رستم = إبراهيم بن رستم أبو بكر المروزي تفقه على محمد وروى عن أبي عصمة نوح الجامع، وسمع من مالك وغيره، وروى عنه أئمة الحديث كأبي عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل وغيره من آثاره النوادر كتبها عن محمد، مات سنة (٢۱۱هـ) اهـ. الفوائد البهية (ص ۲۷).
٢٥- ابن سماعة = محمد بن سماعة بن عبد الله بن هلال بن وكيع أبو عبد الله التميمي ولد سنة (١٣٠هـ)، حـدث عــن الليث بن سعد، وأبي يوسف ومحمد و ـد، وأخذ الفقه عنهما وعن الحسن بن زياد، توفي سنة (۲۳۳هـ ) من آثاره: أدب القاضي، المحاضر والسجلات، النوادر اهـ الفوائد البهية (۲۸۰). ٢٦- ابن سيرين = محمد بن سيرين: هو الإمام محمد بن سيرين، أبو بكر الأنصاري مولى أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه توفي سنة (١١٠هـ) اهـ شذرات الذهب (۱۳۸/۱). ۲۷- ابن شجاع = محمد بن شجاع الثلجي أبو عبد الله توفي سنة (٢٦٦هـ) من آثاره: النوادر، وتصحيح الآثـار اهـ.
الفوائد البهية (۲۸۱)
۲۸- ابن عدي = عبد الله بن عدي الجرجاني: الإمام الحافظ الناقد صاحب كتاب الكامل في الجرح والتعديل ولد سنة (٢۷۷هـ) وتوفي سنة (٣٦٥هـ) اهـ. السير (١٥٤/١٦). ۲۹- ابن عيينة - سفيان بن عيينة بن ميمون الهلالي أبو محمد، محدث، فقيه من آثاره: تفسير القرآن الكريم، الجامع في الحديث، ولد سنة (١٠٧هـ) وتوفي سنة (١٩٦هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٣٥/٤). ٣٠ ابن غانم المقدسي = علي بن محمد المقدسي نور الدين علي بن محمد بن علي الخزرجي بن غانم المقدسي أحد أكابر الفقهاء ولد في القاهرة وتوفي فيها سنة ( ١٠٠٤هـ) اهـ الأعلام (٦٩٦/٢). ۳۱- ابن فارس - الإمام العلامة اللغوي المحدث أبو الحسين أحمد بن فارس بن زكريا بن محمد المعروف بالرازي صاحب كتاب المجمل، المتوفى سنة (٣٩٥هـ ) .ا.هـ السير (١٠٣/١٧).
۳۲- ابن قتيبة - عبد الله بن مسلم بن قتيبة الدينوري أبو محمد، لغوي، نحوي، من تصانيفه: أدب الكاتب، غريب القرآن، ولد سنة (٢١٣هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٧٦هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٥٠/٦).
- ٧٣٦ -
ابن
قدامة - عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمد بن قدامة المقدسي الحنبلي أبو محمد موفق الدين، من تصانيفه: المغني، البرهان في علوم القرآن، ولد سنة (٥٤١هـ ) وتوفي سنة (٦٢٠هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٣٠/٦). ٣٤ ابن قيم الجوزية = محمد بن أبي بكر : هو الإمام محمد بن أبي بكر بن أيوب الزرعي الدمشقي شمس الدين المعروف بـ ( ابن قيم الجوزية) توفي سنة (٧٥١هـ ) اهـ. الأعلام (۸۷۱/۳). ٣٥- ابن كثير - عبد الله بن كثير بن عمرو بن عبد الله بن هرمز، مقرئ مكة المكرمة وأحد القراء السبعة، ولد سنة (٤٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (١٢٠هـ) ا.هـ السير (٣١٨/٥). ٣٦- ابن كج = يوسف بن أحمد بن كج الشافعي، القاضي أبو القاسم الدينوري، من تصانيفه: التجريد. توفي سنة (٤٠٥هـ ) الطبقات الشافعية (۱۹۸/۲).
۳۷- ابن كمال باشا = أحمد بن سليمان الرومي، من تصانيفه: الإصلاح والإيضاح ، توفي سنة (٩٤٠هـ ) ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (٤٤). ۳۸- ابن ماجه - محمد بن يزيد بن ماجه الربعي بالولاء أبو عبد الله، محدث، مفسر، من تصانيفه: كتاب السنن، تفسیر القرآن، ولد سنة (٢٠٩هـ) وتوفي سنة (٢٢٣هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١١٥/١٢). ۳۹- ابن مالك - محمد بن عبد الله بن مالك الطائي الأندلسي الجياني أبو عبد الله النحوي اللغوي شارك في الفقه والأصول والحديث من تصانيفه: إكمال الأعلام بمثلث الكلام، تسهيل الفوائد وتكميل المقاصد ولد سنة (٦٠٠هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٧٢هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٣٤/١٠).
٤٠ - ابن ملك - عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز الشهير بابن ملك، فقيه، أصولي، صوفي، من تصانيفه: شرح كتاب المنار، مبارق الأزهار شرح مشارق الأنوار، توفي سنة (۸۰۱هـ) ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (۱۸۱). ٤١- ابن هشام - عبد الله بن يوسف بن أحمد بن عبد الله بن هشام الأنصاري جمال الدين أبو محمد النحوي شارك في المعاني والبيان والعروض من تصانيفه قطر الندى وبل الصدى مغني اللبيب ولد سنة (۷۰۸هـ) وتوفي سنة (٧٦١هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (١٣٦/٦). ٤٢- ابن وهبان = عبد الوهاب بن أحمد بن وهبان قاضي القضاة أبو محمد الدمشقي ولد قبل ثلاثين وسبعمائة وتوفي سنة (٧٦٨هـ)، من تصانيفه : المنظومة ضمنها غرائب المسائل في مذهب الحنفية، وشرحها في مجلدين وهـو نـظـم جـيـد متمكن اهـ. الفوائد البهية (۱۹۱). ٤٣- أبو الأسود - ظالم بن عمرو بن سفيان بن جندل الدولي، واضع علم النحو، فقيه، شاعر. من تصانيفه: ديوان شعر، ولد سنة (٦٦ق.هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٩هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٤٧/٥). ٤٤- أبو الحسن البكري - محمد بن عبد الرحمن البكري الصديقي، أبو الحسن، صوفي، مفسر، ناظم، من تصانيفه: تحفة واهب المواهب، الواضح الوجيز في تفسير القرآن العزيز، ولد سنة (٨٩٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (٩٥٢هـ ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (۱۳۷۱). ٤٥ - أبو العباس القرطبي = أحمد بن عمر بن إبراهيم بن عمر القرطبي، يعرف في بلاده بابن المزين، محدث، فقیه، من تصانيفه: مختصر الصحيحين، كشف القناع عن الوجد والسماع، ولد سنة (٥٧٨هـ) وتوفي سنة (٦٥٦هـ) ا.هـ معجم المؤلفين (٢٧/٢). ٤٦- أبو الليث = نصر بن محمد السمرقندي: أبو الليث فقيه ،مفسر، محدث، حافظ، توفي سنة (٣٧٥هـ) من تصانيفه: النوازل، خزانة الفقه اهـ. السير (٣٢٢/١٦). ٤٧ - أبو المطيع = الحكم بن عبد الله: هو الإمام الحكم بن عبد الله بن مسلمة بن عبد الرحمـن القـاضـي أبـو مطيـع البلخي، راوي الفقه الأكبر عن أبي حنيفة، توفي سنة (۱۹۹هـ) اهـ. الفوائد البهية (۱۱۸). ٤٨- أبو اليسر البزدوي = محمد بن محمد البزدوي: أبو اليسر انتهت إليه مشيخة الحنفية، توفي سنة (٤٩٣هـ) من تصانيفه: المبسوط اهـ. هدية العارفين (۷۷/۲). ٤٩- أبو بكر الفضلي - محمد بن الفضل الكماري = ابن الفضل. أبو بكر الكماري محمد بن الفضل الكماري = ابن الفضل.
.0-
٥١- أبو بكر الوراق - أحمد بن علي أبو بكر الوراق من تصانيفه: شرح مختصر الطحاوي ا.هـ الفوائد البهية (٥٢).
He took fiqh from:
17- Ibn al-Fadl = Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Kamari: He was a great imam and eminent shaykh, and fatwa books are filled with his fatwas and narrations. Born (426 AH) died (508 AH). End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (303).
18- Ibn al-Qattan = Yahya ibn Sa'id ibn Farukh al-Qattan Abu Sa'id, Commander of the Faithful in Hadith, born (120 AH) died (198 AH). End. al-Siyar (9/175).
19- Ibn al-Najjar = Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn Harun al-Tamimi known as Ibn al-Najjar Abu al-Husayn, literary scholar, grammarian, historian. Works: Tarikh al-Kufa, Mukhtasar fi al-Nahw. Born (303 AH) died (460 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (9/157).
20- Ibn al-Humam = Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid, he is Imam Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahid al-Siwasi known as Ibn al-Humam, commentator on al-Hidayah, naming his work Fath al-Qadir li al-'Ajiz al-Faqir. Died (861 AH). End. Kashf al-Zunun (2/2034).
21- Ibn Hajar = Ahmad ibn 'Ali, he is Imam Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn 'Ali ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani, the hafiz and historian. Born (773 AH) died (852 AH). Works: Fath al-Bari bi Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari, al-Isaba fi Tamyiz al-Sahaba, etc. End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/20).
22- Ibn Khuzayma = Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Khuzayma Abu Bakr, muhaddith. Works: Sahih Ibn Khuzayma, al-Tawhid wa Ithbat Sifat al-Rabb. Born (223 AH) died (311 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (9/39).
23- Ibn Dastawayh = 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far ibn Dastawayh ibn al-Marzban Abu Muhammad, grammarian and linguist. He studied literature under Ibn Qutayba and al-Mubarrad. Works: al-Irshad fi al-Nahw, al-Maqsur wa al-Mamdud, Akhbar al-Nahwiyyin. Born (258 AH) died (347 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (6/40).
24- Ibn Rustam = Ibrahim ibn Rustam Abu Bakr al-Marwazi. He studied fiqh under Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and narrated from Abu 'Isma Nuh al-Jami', and heard from Malik and others. The imams of Hadith like Abu 'Abdullah Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others narrated from him. His works include al-Nawadir written from Muhammad. Died (211 AH). End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (p. 27).
25- Ibn Sama'a = Muhammad ibn Sama'a ibn 'Abdullah ibn Hilal ibn Waki' Abu 'Abdullah al-Tamimi. Born (130 AH). He narrated from al-Layth ibn Sa'd, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and took fiqh from them and from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. Died (233 AH). Works: Adab al-Qadi, al-Mahadir wa al-Sijillat, al-Nawadir. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (280).
26- Ibn Sirin = Muhammad ibn Sirin: He is Imam Muhammad ibn Sirin, Abu Bakr al-Ansari, client of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him). Died (110 AH). End. Shadharat al-Dhahab (1/138).
27- Ibn Shuja' = Muhammad ibn Shuja' al-Thalji Abu 'Abdullah. Died (266 AH). Works: al-Nawadir, Tashih al-Athar. End.
 al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (281)
28- Ibn 'Adiyy = 'Abdullah ibn 'Adiyy al-Jurjani: the imam, hafiz, critic, author of al-Kamil fi al-Jarh wa al-Ta'dil. Born (277 AH) died (365 AH). End. al-Siyar (16/154).
29- Ibn 'Uyayna = Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna ibn Maymun al-Hilali Abu Muhammad, muhaddith, faqih. Works: Tafsir al-Qur'an al-Karim, al-Jami' fi al-Hadith. Born (107 AH) died (196 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (4/235).
30- Ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi = 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Maqdisi, Nur al-Din 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn 'Ali al-Khazraji ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi, one of the major fuqaha. Born in Cairo and died there in (1004 AH). End. al-A'lam (2/696).
31- Ibn Faris = the imam, the brilliant linguist and muhaddith Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Faris ibn Zakariyya ibn Muhammad known as al-Razi, author of Mujmal al-Lugha. Died (395 AH). End. al-Siyar (17/103).
32- Ibn Qutayba = 'Abdullah ibn Muslim ibn Qutayba al-Dinawari Abu Muhammad, linguist, grammarian. Works: Adab al-Katib, Gharib al-Qur'an. Born (213 AH) died (276 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (6/150).
- 736 -
Ibn Qudama = 'Abdullah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Qudama al-Maqdisi al-Hanbali Abu Muhammad Muwaffaq al-Din. Works: al-Mughni, al-Burhan fi 'Ulum al-Qur'an. Born (541 AH) died (620 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (6/30).
34- Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya = Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr: He is Imam Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr ibn Ayyub al-Zur'i al-Dimashqi Shams al-Din known as (Ibn Qayyim al-Jawziyya). Died (751 AH). End. al-A'lam (3/871).
35- Ibn Kathir = 'Abdullah ibn Kathir ibn 'Amr ibn 'Abdullah ibn Hurmuz, reciter of Makkah al-Mukarrama and one of the seven Qira'at. Born (48 AH) died (120 AH). End. al-Siyar (5/318).
36- Ibn Kujj = Yusuf ibn Ahmad ibn Kujj al-Shafi'i, al-Qadi Abu al-Qasim al-Dinawari. Works: al-Tajrid. Died (405 AH). al-Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya (2/198).
37- Ibn Kamal Pasha = Ahmad ibn Sulayman al-Rumi. Works: al-Islah wa al-Idah. Died (940 AH). End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (44).
38- Ibn Majah = Muhammad ibn Yazid ibn Majah al-Rabi'i by wala' Abu 'Abdullah, muhaddith, mufassir. Works: Kitab al-Sunan, Tafsir al-Qur'an. Born (209 AH) died (223 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (12/115).
39- Ibn Malik = Muhammad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Malik al-Ta'i al-Andalusi al-Jiyani Abu 'Abdullah, grammarian and linguist. He participated in fiqh, usul, and hadith. Works: Ikmal al-A'lam bi Muthallath al-Kalam, Tashil al-Fawa'id wa Takmil al-Maqasid. Born (600 AH) died (672 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (10/234).
40- Ibn Malik = 'Abd al-Latif ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz famous as Ibn Malik, faqih, usuli, sufi. Works: Sharh Kitab al-Manar, Mubariq al-Azhar Sharh Mashariq al-Anwar. Died (801 AH). End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (181).
41- Ibn Hisham = 'Abdullah ibn Yusuf ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abdullah ibn Hisham al-Ansari Jamal al-Din Abu Muhammad, grammarian. He participated in ma'ani, bayan, and 'arud. Works: Qatr al-Nada wa Ball al-Sada, Mughni al-Labib. Born (708 AH) died (761 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (6/136).
42- Ibn Wahban = 'Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad ibn Wahban Qadi al-Qudat Abu Muhammad al-Dimashqi. Born slightly before 730 and died in (768 AH). Works: al-Manzuma comprising rare issues in the Hanafi madhhab, and its commentary in two volumes. It is good, skilled poetry. End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (191).
43- Abu al-Aswad = Zalim ibn 'Amr ibn Sufyan ibn Jandal al-Du'ali, founder of Arabic grammar, faqih, poet. Works: Diwan Shi'r. Born (66 years before Hijra) died (69 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (5/47).
44- Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri = Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Bakri al-Siddiqi, Abu al-Hasan, sufi, mufassir, poet. Works: Tuhfat Wahib al-Mawahib, al-Wadih al-Wajiz fi Tafsir al-Qur'an al-'Aziz. Born (898 AH) died (952 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (13/71).
45- Abu al-'Abbas al-Qurtubi = Ahmad ibn 'Umar ibn Ibrahim ibn 'Umar al-Qurtubi, known in his land as Ibn al-Muzayyin, muhaddith, faqih. Works: Mukhtasar al-Sahihayn, Kashf al-Qina' 'an al-Wajd wa al-Sama'. Born (578 AH) died (656 AH). End. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/27).
46- Abu al-Layth = Nasr ibn Muhammad al-Samarqandi: Abu al-Layth, faqih, mufassir, muhaddith, hafiz. Died (375 AH). Works: al-Nawazil, Khizanat al-Fiqh. End. al-Siyar (16/322).
47- Abu al-Muti' = al-Hakam ibn 'Abdullah: He is Imam al-Hakam ibn 'Abdullah ibn Muslima ibn 'Abd al-Rahman, al-Qadi Abu Muti' al-Balkhi, transmitter of al-Fiqh al-Akbar from Abu Hanifa. Died (199 AH). End. al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya (118).
48- Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi = Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi: Abu al-Yusr, the shaykh of the Hanafis in his time. Died (493 AH). Works: al-Mabsut. End. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin (2/77).
49- Abu Bakr al-Fadli = Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Kamari = Ibn al-Fadl. Abu Bakr al-Kamari Muhammad ibn al-Fadl al-Kamari = Ibn al-Fadl.
